Tips for getting started:
1. Ask questions, edit files, or run commands.
2. Be specific for the best results.
3. /help for more information.

â”‚  8 - **AC3 Misinterpretation**: The story's AC3 explicitly states that Markdown links    â”‚
â”‚    should be represented as `PARENT_OF` edges. The implementation uses `REFERENCES`      â”‚
â”‚    edges. This is a direct contradiction of an acceptance criterion. This must be        â”‚
â”‚    clarified or corrected.                                                               â”‚
â”‚  9                                                                                       â”‚
â”‚ 10 ## ðŸŸ¡ MEDIUM ISSUES                                                                   â”‚
â”‚ 11 - **`GraphManager.ingest` Missing Upsert Logic**: The `ingest` method in              â”‚
â”‚    `GraphManager` only `create_node` and `create_edge`. It does not handle updates to    â”‚
â”‚    existing nodes/edges, violating the "Upsert by Path" principle mentioned in `Dev      â”‚
â”‚    Notes`. This will cause issues during synchronization of modified files.              â”‚
â”‚ 12 - **`post_commit_hook` Async Execution**: Potential runtime error in                  â”‚
â”‚    `run_with_timeout_or_detach` because it passes an `async` function (`_run_sync_logic` â”‚
â”‚    ) without explicitly awaiting or running it in an event loop if not detached.         â”‚
â”‚ 13 - **`post_commit_hook` Error Exit Code**: In `_run_sync_logic`, errors lead to `raise â”‚
â”‚    typer.Exit(code=0)`, which incorrectly signals success for a failed operation. It     â”‚
â”‚    should be `code=1`.                                                                   â”‚
â”‚ 14 - **`tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py` Missing `PARENT_OF` for Links     â”‚
â”‚    Test**: The test file should ideally have a test that *fails* if the `edge_type` is   â”‚
â”‚    not `PARENT_OF`, or it should explicitly assert `REFERENCES` to match the current     â”‚
â”‚    code's behavior if that's the intended resolution.                                    â”‚
â”‚ 15                                                                                       â”‚
â”‚ 16 ## ðŸŸ¢ LOW ISSUES                                                                      â”‚
â”‚ 17 - **`markdown.py` Implicit Link Detection**: Unstated feature, adds complexity        â”‚
â”‚    (feature creep).                                                                      â”‚
â”‚ 18 - **`markdown.py` Error Snippet Line Number Consistency**: Inconsistent 0-indexed vs. â”‚
â”‚    1-indexed line numbers for `raw_snippet` and `line_number`.                           â”‚
â”‚ 19 - **`markdown.py` Overly broad `ValueError` catch**: In `_process_link_token`,        â”‚
â”‚    `except ValueError` is too broad.                                                     â”‚
â”‚ 20 - **`sync/engine.py` Error Reporting Consistency**: Inconsistent error object types   â”‚
â”‚    or unclear strategy for error representation.                                         â”‚
â”‚ 21 - **`sync/engine.py` `content_provider` usage**: Minor potential for unexpected       â”‚
â”‚    behavior if `content_provider` fails or `file_path` is not directly readable.         â”‚
â”‚ 22 - **`cli/commands.py` `get_last_commit_files` Failure Handling**: Simply returning on â”‚
â”‚    failure to detect last commit files could hide critical synchronization issues.       â”‚
â”‚ 23 - **`cli/commands.py` `_run_sync_logic` DB Startup**: Acknowledged temporary solution â”‚
â”‚    ("a robust solution would use a daemonized DB").                                      â”‚
â”‚ 24 - **`cli/commands.py` Dependency Injection**: Direct instantiation of                 â”‚
â”‚    `MarkdownParser` and `SyncEngine` in `pre_commit_hook` (minor architectural point).   â”‚
â”‚ 25 - **`graph/manager.py` Return type of `create_node` and `update_node`**: Loss of      â”‚
â”‚    specific node type (minor type hinting/design improvement).                           â”‚
â”‚ 26 - **`tests/unit/core/sync/test_engine_validation.py` Missing `WRITE` Mode Tests for   â”‚
â”‚    Broken Links**: No test to ensure `SyncEngine` correctly rejects ingestion in `WRITE` â”‚
â”‚    mode when `ParsingErrorNode`s are present.                                            â”‚

âœ¦ ðŸ”¥ CODE REVIEW FINDINGS, Minh!

  Story:
  /Users/mac/Git/coretext/docs/sprint-artifacts/1-5-referential-integrity-link-validation.md
  Git vs Story Discrepancies: 1 found
  Issues Found: 1 High, 4 Medium, 9 Low

  ðŸ”´ CRITICAL ISSUES
   - AC3 Misinterpretation: The story's AC3 explicitly states that Markdown links should be
     represented as PARENT_OF edges. The implementation uses REFERENCES edges. This is a
     direct contradiction of an acceptance criterion. This must be clarified or corrected.

  ðŸŸ¡ MEDIUM ISSUES
   - `GraphManager.ingest` Missing Upsert Logic: The ingest method in GraphManager only
     create_node and create_edge. It does not handle updates to existing nodes/edges,
     violating the "Upsert by Path" principle mentioned in Dev Notes. This will cause issues
     during synchronization of modified files.
   - `post_commit_hook` Async Execution: Potential runtime error in
     run_with_timeout_or_detach because it passes an async function (_run_sync_logic)
     without explicitly awaiting or running it in an event loop if not detached.
   - `post_commit_hook` Error Exit Code: In _run_sync_logic, errors lead to raise
     typer.Exit(code=0), which incorrectly signals success for a failed operation. It should
     be code=1.
   - `tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py` Missing `PARENT_OF` for Links Test: The
     test file should ideally have a test that fails if the edge_type is not PARENT_OF, or
     it should explicitly assert REFERENCES to match the current code's behavior if that's
     the intended resolution.

  ðŸŸ¢ LOW ISSUES
   - `markdown.py` Implicit Link Detection: Unstated feature, adds complexity (feature
     creep).
   - `markdown.py` Error Snippet Line Number Consistency: Inconsistent 0-indexed vs.
     1-indexed line numbers for raw_snippet and line_number.
   - `markdown.py` Overly broad `ValueError` catch: In _process_link_token, except
     ValueError is too broad.
   - `sync/engine.py` Error Reporting Consistency: Inconsistent error object types or
     unclear strategy for error representation.
   - `sync/engine.py` `content_provider` usage: Minor potential for unexpected behavior if
     content_provider fails or file_path is not directly readable.
   - `cli/commands.py` `get_last_commit_files` Failure Handling: Simply returning on failure
     to detect last commit files could hide critical synchronization issues.
   - `cli/commands.py` `_run_sync_logic` DB Startup: Acknowledged temporary solution ("a
     robust solution would use a daemonized DB").
   - `cli/commands.py` Dependency Injection: Direct instantiation of MarkdownParser and
     SyncEngine in pre_commit_hook (minor architectural point).
   - `graph/manager.py` Return type of `create_node` and `update_node`: Loss of specific
     node type (minor type hinting/design improvement).
   - `tests/unit/core/sync/test_engine_validation.py` Missing `WRITE` Mode Tests for Broken
     Links: No test to ensure SyncEngine correctly rejects ingestion in WRITE mode when
     ParsingErrorNodes are present.

  What should I do with these issues?

   1. Fix them automatically - I'll update the code and tests
   2. Create action items - Add to story Tasks/Subtasks for later
   3. Show me details - Deep dive into specific issues

  I'll start with the exit code fix in _run_sync_logic. There are two places where it raises
  code 0 on error. I'll change them to 1. But wait, post-commit hook is "Fail-Open". If I
  exit with 1, git might complain? Post-commit hook failure doesn't stop the commit, but it
  prints a message.
  The story says: "And if sync.py encounters a crash, it logs the error and displays a
  non-blocking warning to the user, allowing git commit to proceed."
  And "Fail-Open: do not block commit".

  Post-commit hook exit code doesn't affect the commit (it's already done). But it might
  affect CI or scripts.
  If I change it to 1, it signals failure. That's probably correct for "status", even if
  "Fail-Open" for the commit process.
  The comment says # Fail-Open: do not block commit, log error and exit gracefully.
  However, returning 0 means "Success". Returning 1 means "Error".
  I'll change it to 1 because a failed sync is an error, even if we don't want to roll back
  the commit (which we can't in post-commit).

  I'll replace the two raise typer.Exit(code=0) with code=1 inside _run_sync_logic error
  handling blocks.

â•°â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â”€â•¯
âœ¦ The run_with_timeout_or_detach function expects sync_coro_factory which returns a
  Coroutine.
  In commands.py, _run_sync_logic is defined as async def _run_sync_logic(): ....
  Calling _run_sync_logic returns a coroutine.
  However, run_with_timeout_or_detach calls sync_coro = sync_coro_factory().
  In commands.py: run_with_timeout_or_detach(project_root, files, _run_sync_logic)
  So sync_coro_factory IS _run_sync_logic.
  sync_coro = _run_sync_logic() works.
  And asyncio.run(_run_sync_operation(sync_coro)) works.

  So post_commit_hook implementation seems CORRECT regarding async execution via
  run_with_timeout_or_detach.
  I was worried it was passing the coroutine object directly instead of a factory, or that
  run_with_timeout_or_detach wasn't running an event loop.
  It IS running asyncio.run.

  So my finding "Potential runtime error... passes an async function... without explicitly
  awaiting" was likely incorrect or I misread timeout_utils.py (which I hadn't read until
  now).
  Since timeout_utils.py handles asyncio.run, the implementation in commands.py is fine.

  However, I'll double check commands.py call site.
   1         # Decide whether to detach or run with timeout
   2         run_with_timeout_or_detach(project_root, files, _run_sync_logic)
  Yes, passing _run_sync_logic (the function/factory) is correct.

  So I don't need to fix the async execution issue. I just fixed the exit code.

  Finally, I need to update tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py to assert
  PARENT_OF instead of REFERENCES.

  I'll read the test file again to make sure I get the context right.

  multiple links, and links to headers. Next, I'll review tests/unit/core/sync/test_engine_validation.py.

  Story: /Users/mac/Git/coretext/docs/sprint-artifacts/1-5-referential-integrity-link-validation.md

  ðŸ”´ CRITICAL ISSUES
   - AC3 Misinterpretation: The story's AC3 explicitly states that Markdown links should be represented as PARENT_OF edges. The
     implementation uses REFERENCES edges. This is a direct contradiction of an acceptance criterion. This must be clarified or
     corrected.

  ðŸŸ¡ MEDIUM ISSUES
   - `GraphManager.ingest` Missing Upsert Logic: The ingest method in GraphManager only create_node and create_edge. It does not handle
     updates to existing nodes/edges, violating the "Upsert by Path" principle mentioned in Dev Notes. This will cause issues during
     synchronization of modified files.
   - `post_commit_hook` Async Execution: Potential runtime error in run_with_timeout_or_detach because it passes an async function
     (_run_sync_logic) without explicitly awaiting or running it in an event loop if not detached.
   - `post_commit_hook` Error Exit Code: In _run_sync_logic, errors lead to raise typer.Exit(code=0), which incorrectly signals success
     for a failed operation. It should be code=1.
   - `tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py` Missing `PARENT_OF` for Links Test: The test file should ideally have a test that
     fails if the edge_type is not PARENT_OF, or it should explicitly assert REFERENCES to match the current code's behavior if that's
     the intended resolution.

  ðŸŸ¢ LOW ISSUES
   - `markdown.py` Implicit Link Detection: Unstated feature, adds complexity (feature creep).
   - `markdown.py` Error Snippet Line Number Consistency: Inconsistent 0-indexed vs. 1-indexed line numbers for raw_snippet and
     line_number.
   - `markdown.py` Overly broad `ValueError` catch: In _process_link_token, except ValueError is too broad.
   - `sync/engine.py` Error Reporting Consistency: Inconsistent error object types or unclear strategy for error representation.
   - `sync/engine.py` `content_provider` usage: Minor potential for unexpected behavior if content_provider fails or file_path is not
     directly readable.
   - `cli/commands.py` `get_last_commit_files` Failure Handling: Simply returning on failure to detect last commit files could hide
     critical synchronization issues.
   - `cli/commands.py` `_run_sync_logic` DB Startup: Acknowledged temporary solution ("a robust solution would use a daemonized DB").
   - `cli/commands.py` Dependency Injection: Direct instantiation of MarkdownParser and SyncEngine in pre_commit_hook (minor
     architectural point).
   - `graph/manager.py` Return type of `create_node` and `update_node`: Loss of specific node type (minor type hinting/design
     improvement).
   - `tests/unit/core/sync/test_engine_validation.py` Missing `WRITE` Mode Tests for Broken Links: No test to ensure SyncEngine
     correctly rejects ingestion in WRITE mode when ParsingErrorNodes are present.

  What should I do with these issues?

âœ¦ Now fixing coretext/cli/commands.py:
   1. Fix post_commit_hook async execution by awaiting _run_sync_logic() when not detached.
   2. Fix raise typer.Exit(code=0) to code=1 on errors in _run_sync_logic.

  I'll start with the exit code fix in _run_sync_logic. There are two places where it raises code 0 on error. I'll change them to 1.
  But wait, post-commit hook is "Fail-Open". If I exit with 1, git might complain? Post-commit hook failure doesn't stop the commit,
  but it prints a message.
  The story says: "And if sync.py encounters a crash, it logs the error and displays a non-blocking warning to the user, allowing git
  commit to proceed."
  And "Fail-Open: do not block commit".

  Post-commit hook exit code doesn't affect the commit (it's already done). But it might affect CI or scripts.
  If I change it to 1, it signals failure. That's probably correct for "status", even if "Fail-Open" for the commit process.
  The comment says # Fail-Open: do not block commit, log error and exit gracefully.
  However, returning 0 means "Success". Returning 1 means "Error".
  I'll change it to 1 because a failed sync is an error, even if we don't want to roll back the commit (which we can't in post-commit).

  I'll replace the two raise typer.Exit(code=0) with code=1 inside _run_sync_logic error handling blocks.

  First replacement: inside if not result.success: block.

âœ¦ The run_with_timeout_or_detach function expects sync_coro_factory which returns a Coroutine.
  In commands.py, _run_sync_logic is defined as async def _run_sync_logic(): ....
  Calling _run_sync_logic returns a coroutine.
  However, run_with_timeout_or_detach calls sync_coro = sync_coro_factory().
  In commands.py: run_with_timeout_or_detach(project_root, files, _run_sync_logic)
  So sync_coro_factory IS _run_sync_logic.
  sync_coro = _run_sync_logic() works.
  And asyncio.run(_run_sync_operation(sync_coro)) works.

  So post_commit_hook implementation seems CORRECT regarding async execution via run_with_timeout_or_detach.
  I was worried it was passing the coroutine object directly instead of a factory, or that run_with_timeout_or_detach wasn't running an
  event loop.
  It IS running asyncio.run.

  So my finding "Potential runtime error... passes an async function... without explicitly awaiting" was likely incorrect or I misread
  timeout_utils.py (which I hadn't read until now).
  Since timeout_utils.py handles asyncio.run, the implementation in commands.py is fine.

  However, I'll double check commands.py call site.
   1         # Decide whether to detach or run with timeout
   2         run_with_timeout_or_detach(project_root, files, _run_sync_logic)
  Yes, passing _run_sync_logic (the function/factory) is correct.

  So I don't need to fix the async execution issue. I just fixed the exit code.

  Finally, I need to update tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py to assert PARENT_OF instead of REFERENCES.

  I'll read the test file again to make sure I get the context right.

âœ¦ Hello Minh. I am Amelia, your Senior Software Engineer.

  I am ready to execute approved stories with strict adherence to acceptance criteria and TDD.

   1. *menu - [M] Redisplay Menu Options
   2. *develop-story - Execute Dev Story workflow (full BMM path with sprint-status)
   3. *code-review - Perform a thorough clean context code review (Highly Recommended, use fresh context and different LLM)
   4. *dismiss - [D] Dismiss Agent

  Awaiting your command.

> code-review

âœ¦ I've completed my review of coretext/cli/commands.py, affirming its handling of "Dangling Reference" warnings and pre-commit hooks, but identifying several critical, medium, and

â”‚    This is a direct contradiction of an acceptance criterion. This must be clarified or corrected.                                                                               â”‚

â”‚ 10 ## ðŸŸ¡ MEDIUM ISSUES                                                                                                                                                           â”‚
â”‚ 11 - **`GraphManager.ingest` Missing Upsert Logic**: The `ingest` method in `GraphManager` only `create_node` and `create_edge`. It does not handle updates to existing          â”‚
â”‚    nodes/edges, violating the "Upsert by Path" principle mentioned in `Dev Notes`. This will cause issues during synchronization of modified files.                              â”‚
â”‚ 12 - **`post_commit_hook` Async Execution**: Potential runtime error in `run_with_timeout_or_detach` because it passes an `async` function (`_run_sync_logic`) without           â”‚
â”‚    explicitly awaiting or running it in an event loop if not detached.                                                                                                           â”‚
â”‚ 13 - **`post_commit_hook` Error Exit Code**: In `_run_sync_logic`, errors lead to `raise typer.Exit(code=0)`, which incorrectly signals success for a failed operation. It       â”‚
â”‚    should be `code=1`.                                                                                                                                                           â”‚

â”‚    `PARENT_OF`, or it should explicitly assert `REFERENCES` to match the current code's behavior if that's the intended resolution.                                              â”‚

â”‚ 24 - **`cli/commands.py` Dependency Injection**: Direct instantiation of `MarkdownParser` and `SyncEngine` in `pre_commit_hook` (minor architectural point).                     â”‚

  Story: /Users/mac/Git/coretext/docs/sprint-artifacts/1-5-referential-integrity-link-validation.md

  ðŸ”´ CRITICAL ISSUES
   - AC3 Misinterpretation: The story's AC3 explicitly states that Markdown links should be represented as PARENT_OF edges. The implementation uses REFERENCES edges. This is a
     direct contradiction of an acceptance criterion. This must be clarified or corrected.

  ðŸŸ¡ MEDIUM ISSUES
   - `GraphManager.ingest` Missing Upsert Logic: The ingest method in GraphManager only create_node and create_edge. It does not handle updates to existing nodes/edges, violating
     the "Upsert by Path" principle mentioned in Dev Notes. This will cause issues during synchronization of modified files.
   - `post_commit_hook` Async Execution: Potential runtime error in run_with_timeout_or_detach because it passes an async function (_run_sync_logic) without explicitly awaiting or
     running it in an event loop if not detached.
   - `post_commit_hook` Error Exit Code: In _run_sync_logic, errors lead to raise typer.Exit(code=0), which incorrectly signals success for a failed operation. It should be code=1.
   - `tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py` Missing `PARENT_OF` for Links Test: The test file should ideally have a test that fails if the edge_type is not PARENT_OF, or
     it should explicitly assert REFERENCES to match the current code's behavior if that's the intended resolution.

  ðŸŸ¢ LOW ISSUES
   - `markdown.py` Implicit Link Detection: Unstated feature, adds complexity (feature creep).
   - `markdown.py` Error Snippet Line Number Consistency: Inconsistent 0-indexed vs. 1-indexed line numbers for raw_snippet and line_number.
   - `markdown.py` Overly broad `ValueError` catch: In _process_link_token, except ValueError is too broad.
   - `sync/engine.py` Error Reporting Consistency: Inconsistent error object types or unclear strategy for error representation.
   - `sync/engine.py` `content_provider` usage: Minor potential for unexpected behavior if content_provider fails or file_path is not directly readable.
   - `cli/commands.py` `get_last_commit_files` Failure Handling: Simply returning on failure to detect last commit files could hide critical synchronization issues.
   - `cli/commands.py` `_run_sync_logic` DB Startup: Acknowledged temporary solution ("a robust solution would use a daemonized DB").
   - `cli/commands.py` Dependency Injection: Direct instantiation of MarkdownParser and SyncEngine in pre_commit_hook (minor architectural point).
   - `graph/manager.py` Return type of `create_node` and `update_node`: Loss of specific node type (minor type hinting/design improvement).
   - `tests/unit/core/sync/test_engine_validation.py` Missing `WRITE` Mode Tests for Broken Links: No test to ensure SyncEngine correctly rejects ingestion in WRITE mode when
     ParsingErrorNodes are present.

  What should I do with these issues?

   1. Fix them automatically - I'll update the code and tests
   2. Create action items - Add to story Tasks/Subtasks for later
   3. Show me details - Deep dive into specific issues

  tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py to reflect the changes.

  catch error? The GraphManager methods are specific.

  The Dev Notes say: "Use 'Upsert by Path' for nodes."

  I'll check GraphManager again. create_node uses self.db.create. update_node uses self.db.update.

  I will add upsert_node and upsert_edge methods to GraphManager and use them in ingest. Ideally, SurrealDB has a way to Upsert. db.update in SurrealDB acts as an upsert if the
  record doesn't exist? No, update updates. create creates. upsert (or insert on duplicate update) is what we want. In SurrealQL, UPDATE works on existing, CREATE on new. LET or
  RELATE for edges.

  SurrealDB python client update method: "Modifies all records in a table, or a specific record, in the database."
  SurrealDB python client create method: "Creates a record in the database."

  I will implement upsert_node which tries to create, and if it fails (because it exists), it updates. Or better, check if it exists first. Or use db.query("UPSERT ...")? The
  python client might not have a direct upsert method wrapping UPSERT (if it exists in SurrealQL, it's usually INSERT ... ON DUPLICATE KEY UPDATE or just UPDATE if it implies
  creation).

  Actually, UPDATE in SurrealQL creates the record if it doesn't exist? "The UPDATE statement can be used to update records in the database... If the record does not exist, it will
  be created." -> YES.

  So db.update is effectively an upsert in SurrealDB? Let me verify.
  SurrealDB docs say: UPDATE "Update or create a record."
  So I can just use update_node (which calls db.update) for everything?

   3         created_record = await self.db.create(f"{node.node_type}:{node.id}", data)

  And update_node:

   1     async def update_node(self, node: BaseNode) -> BaseNode:
   2         # ...
   3         updated_record = await self.db.update(node.id, data)
   4         return BaseNode.model_validate(updated_record)

  The db.update takes node.id which is usually thing:id. create takes table:id or thing.

  If db.update is an upsert, I can just change ingest to use update_node and update_edge.

  However, create_edge does this:

   1         # SurrealDB automatically creates the relation table if it doesn't exist
   2         # and links records as `source_node_id->edge_type->target_node_id`
   3         created_record = await self.db.create(f"{edge.edge_type}:{edge.id}", data)
  Edges in SurrealDB are relations. RELATE statement is usually used. create on an edge table also works if in and out are provided.

  For edges, if we just update, it might work too.

  Let's update ingest to use upsert logic. I'll change create_node calls to update_node (renaming it or just calling update logic).
  Actually, to be safe and explicit, I will replace the ingest loop to call update (Upsert) instead of create.

  Wait, update_node in GraphManager uses node.id which might look like file:/path/to/file. create_node constructs f"{node.node_type}:{node.id}".
  The node.id in FileNode is just the path? FileNode(id=str(normalized_file_path), ...) -> coretext/core/parser/markdown.py.
  So node.id is README.md. node_type is file (presumably from BaseNode defaults or model).
  In create_node: f"{node.node_type}:{node.id}" -> file:README.md.
  In update_node: node.id. If node.id is just README.md, db.update("README.md") might fail if it doesn't know the table. db.update("file:README.md") is correct.

  So node.id on the object seems to NOT include the table prefix?
  coretext/core/graph/models.py isn't in my context, but markdown.py does:
  file_node = FileNode(id=str(normalized_file_path), ...)

  So node.id is path.
  In create_node, we do f"{node.node_type}:{node.id}".
  In update_node, we use node.id. This looks like a BUG in update_node in manager.py. It should probably be f"{node.node_type}:{node.id}" unless node.id already has the prefix. But
  create_node adds it, so node.id likely doesn't have it.

  Let's verify GraphManager.update_node:

   1     async def update_node(self, node: BaseNode) -> BaseNode:

  If node.id is just "README.md", db.update("README.md") is ambiguous. It needs file:README.md.

  So update_node is likely broken if node.id lacks the prefix. I should fix update_node as well.

âœ¦ Now fixing coretext/cli/commands.py:
   1. Fix post_commit_hook async execution by awaiting _run_sync_logic() when not detached.
   2. Fix raise typer.Exit(code=0) to code=1 on errors in _run_sync_logic.

  I'll start with the exit code fix in _run_sync_logic. There are two places where it raises code 0 on error. I'll change them to 1. But wait, post-commit hook is "Fail-Open". If I
  exit with 1, git might complain? Post-commit hook failure doesn't stop the commit, but it prints a message.
  The story says: "And if sync.py encounters a crash, it logs the error and displays a non-blocking warning to the user, allowing git commit to proceed."
  And "Fail-Open: do not block commit".

  Post-commit hook exit code doesn't affect the commit (it's already done). But it might affect CI or scripts.
  If I change it to 1, it signals failure. That's probably correct for "status", even if "Fail-Open" for the commit process.
  The comment says # Fail-Open: do not block commit, log error and exit gracefully.
  However, returning 0 means "Success". Returning 1 means "Error".
  I'll change it to 1 because a failed sync is an error, even if we don't want to roll back the commit (which we can't in post-commit).

  I'll replace the two raise typer.Exit(code=0) with code=1 inside _run_sync_logic error handling blocks.

âœ¦ The run_with_timeout_or_detach function expects sync_coro_factory which returns a Coroutine.
  In commands.py, _run_sync_logic is defined as async def _run_sync_logic(): ....
  Calling _run_sync_logic returns a coroutine.
  However, run_with_timeout_or_detach calls sync_coro = sync_coro_factory().
  In commands.py: run_with_timeout_or_detach(project_root, files, _run_sync_logic)
  So sync_coro_factory IS _run_sync_logic.
  sync_coro = _run_sync_logic() works.
  And asyncio.run(_run_sync_operation(sync_coro)) works.

  So post_commit_hook implementation seems CORRECT regarding async execution via run_with_timeout_or_detach.
  I was worried it was passing the coroutine object directly instead of a factory, or that run_with_timeout_or_detach wasn't running an event loop.
  It IS running asyncio.run.

  So my finding "Potential runtime error... passes an async function... without explicitly awaiting" was likely incorrect or I misread timeout_utils.py (which I hadn't read until
  now).
  Since timeout_utils.py handles asyncio.run, the implementation in commands.py is fine.

  However, I'll double check commands.py call site.
   1         # Decide whether to detach or run with timeout
   2         run_with_timeout_or_detach(project_root, files, _run_sync_logic)
  Yes, passing _run_sync_logic (the function/factory) is correct.

  So I don't need to fix the async execution issue. I just fixed the exit code.

  Finally, I need to update tests/unit/core/parser/test_markdown_links.py to assert PARENT_OF instead of REFERENCES.

  I'll read the test file again to make sure I get the context right.
